   22→\n    23→// [#protodoc-title: External Processing Filter]\n    24→// External Processing Filter\n    25→// [#extension: envoy.filters.http.ext_proc]\n    26→\n    27→// The External Processing filter allows an external service to act on HTTP traffic in a flexible way.\n    28→\n    29→// **Current Implementation Status:**\n    30→// All options and processing modes are implemented except for the following:\n    31→//\n    32→// * \"async mode\" is not implemented.\n    33→\n    34→// The filter communicates with an external gRPC service called an \"external processor\"\n    35→// that can do a variety of things with the request and response:\n    36→//\n    37→// * Access and modify the HTTP headers on the request, response, or both\n    38→// * Access and modify the HTTP request and response bodies\n    39→// * Access and modify the dynamic stream metadata\n    40→// * Immediately send an HTTP response downstream and terminate other processing\n    41→//\n    42→// The filter communicates with the server using a gRPC bidirectional stream. After the initial\n    43→// request, the external server is in control over what additional data is sent to it\n    44→// and how it should be processed.\n    45→//\n    46→// By implementing the protocol specified by the stream, the external server can choose:\n    47→//\n    48→// * Whether it receives the response message at all\n    49→// * Whether it receives the message body at all, in separate chunks, or as a single buffer\n    50→// * Whether subsequent HTTP requests are transmitted synchronously or whether they are\n    51→//   sent asynchronously.\n    52→// * To modify request or response trailers if they already exist\n    53→//\n    54→// The filter supports up to six different processing steps. Each is represented by\n    55→// a gRPC stream message that is sent to the external processor. For each message, the\n    56→// processor must send a matching response.\n    57→//\n    58→// * Request headers: Contains the headers from the original HTTP request.\n    59→// * Request body: Delivered if they are present and sent in a single message if\n    60→//   the BUFFERED or BUFFERED_PARTIAL mode is chosen, in multiple messages if the\n    61→//   STREAMED mode is chosen, and not at all otherwise.\n    62→// * Request trailers: Delivered if they are present and if the trailer mode is set\n    63→//   to SEND.\n    64→// * Response headers: Contains the headers from the HTTP response. Keep in mind\n    65→//   that if the upstream system sends them before processing the request body that\n    66→//   this message may arrive before the complete body.\n    67→// * Response body: Sent according to the processing mode like the request body.\n    68→// * Response trailers: Delivered according to the processing mode like the\n    69→//   request trailers.\n    70→//\n    71→// By default, the processor sends only the request and response headers messages.\n    72→// This may be changed to include any of the six steps by changing the processing_mode\n    73→// setting of the filter configuration, or by setting the mode_override of any response\n    74→// from the external processor. The latter is only enabled if allow_mode_override is\n    75→// set to true. This way, a processor may, for example, use information\n    76→// in the request header to determine whether the message body must be examined, or whether\n    77→// the proxy should simply stream it straight through.\n    78→//\n    79→// All of this together allows a server to process the filter traffic in fairly\n    80→// sophisticated ways. For example:\n    81→//\n    82→// * A server may choose to examine all or part of the HTTP message bodies depending\n    83→//   on the content of the headers.\n    84→// * A server may choose to immediately reject some messages based on their HTTP\n    85→//   headers (or other dynamic metadata) and more carefully examine others.\n    86→// * A server may asynchronously monitor traffic coming through the filter by inspecting\n    87→//   headers, bodies, or both, and then decide to switch to a synchronous processing\n    88→//   mode, either permanently or temporarily.\n    89→//\n    90→// The protocol itself is based on a bidirectional gRPC stream. Envoy will send the\n    91→// server\n    92→// :ref:`ProcessingRequest <envoy_v3_api_msg_service.ext_proc.v3.ProcessingRequest>`\n    93→// messages, and the server must reply with\n    94→// :ref:`ProcessingResponse <envoy_v3_api_msg_service.ext_proc.v3.ProcessingResponse>`.\n    95→//\n    96→// Stats about each gRPC call are recorded in a :ref:`dynamic filter state\n    97→// <arch_overview_advanced_filter_state_sharing>` object in a namespace matching the filter\n    98→// name.\n    99→//\n   100→// [#next-free-field: 18]\n   101→message ExternalProcessor {\n   102→  reserved 4;\n   103→\n   104→  reserved \"async_mode\";\n   105→\n   106→  // Configuration for the gRPC service that the filter will communicate with.\n   107→  // The filter supports both the \"Envoy\" and \"Google\" gRPC clients.\n   108→  config.core.v3.GrpcService grpc_service = 1 [(validate.rules).message = {required: true}];\n   109→\n   110→  // By default, if the gRPC stream cannot be established, or if it is closed\n   111→  // prematurely with an error, the filter will fail. Specifically, if the\n   112→  // response headers have not yet been delivered, then it will return a 500\n   113→  // error downstream. If they have been delivered, then instead the HTTP stream to the\n   114→  // downstream client will be reset.\n   115→  // With this parameter set to true, however, then if the gRPC stream is prematurely closed\n   116→  // or could not be opened, processing continues without error.\n   117→  bool failure_mode_allow = 2;\n   118→\n   119→  // Specifies default options for how HTTP headers, trailers, and bodies are\n   120→  // sent. See ProcessingMode for details.\n   121→  ProcessingMode processing_mode = 3;\n   122→\n   123→  // Envoy provides a number of :ref:`attributes <arch_overview_attributes>`\n   124→  // for expressive policies. Each attribute name provided in this field will be\n   125→  // matched against that list and populated in the request_headers message.\n   126→  // See the :ref:`attribute documentation <arch_overview_request_attributes>`\n   127→  // for the list of supported attributes and their types.\n   128→  repeated string request_attributes = 5;\n   129→\n   130→  // Envoy provides a number of :ref:`attributes <arch_overview_attributes>`\n   131→  // for expressive policies. Each attribute name provided in this field will be\n   132→  // matched against that list and populated in the response_headers message.\n   133→  // See the :ref:`attribute documentation <arch_overview_attributes>`\n   134→  // for the list of supported attributes and their types.\n   135→  repeated string response_attributes = 6;\n   136→\n   137→  // Specifies the timeout for each individual message sent on the stream and\n   138→  // when the filter is running in synchronous mode. Whenever the proxy sends\n   139→  // a message on the stream that requires a response, it will reset this timer,\n   140→  // and will stop processing and return an error (subject to the processing mode)\n   141→  // if the timer expires before a matching response is received. There is no\n   142→  // timeout when the filter is running in asynchronous mode. Zero is a valid\n   143→  // config which means the timer will be triggered immediately. If not\n   144→  // configured, default is 200 milliseconds.\n   145→  google.protobuf.Duration message_timeout = 7 [(validate.rules).duration = {\n   146→    lte {seconds: 3600}\n   147→    gte {}\n   148→  }];\n   149→\n   150→  // Optional additional prefix to use when emitting statistics. This allows to distinguish\n   151→  // emitted statistics between configured *ext_proc* filters in an HTTP filter chain.\n   152→  string stat_prefix = 8;\n   153→\n   154→  // Rules that determine what modifications an external processing server may\n   155→  // make to message headers. If not set, all headers may be modified except\n   156→  // for \"host\", \":authority\", \":scheme\", \":method\", and headers that start\n   157→  // with the header prefix set via\n   158→  // :ref:`header_prefix <envoy_v3_api_field_config.bootstrap.v3.Bootstrap.header_prefix>`\n   159→  // (which is usually \"x-envoy\").\n   160→  // Note that changing headers such as \"host\" or \":authority\" may not in itself\n   161→  // change Envoy's routing decision, as routes can be cached. To also force the\n   162→  // route to be recomputed, set the\n   163→  // :ref:`clear_route_cache <envoy_v3_api_field_service.ext_proc.v3.CommonResponse.clear_route_cache>`\n   164→  // field to true in the same response.\n   165→  config.common.mutation_rules.v3.HeaderMutationRules mutation_rules = 9;\n   166→\n   167→  // Specify the upper bound of\n   168→  // :ref:`override_message_timeout <envoy_v3_api_field_service.ext_proc.v3.ProcessingResponse.override_message_timeout>`\n   169→  // If not specified, by default it is 0, which will effectively disable the ``override_message_timeout`` API.\n   170→  google.protobuf.Duration max_message_timeout = 10 [(validate.rules).duration = {\n   171→    lte {seconds: 3600}\n   172→    gte {}\n   173→  }];\n   174→\n   175→  // Prevents clearing the route-cache when the\n   176→  // :ref:`clear_route_cache <envoy_v3_api_field_service.ext_proc.v3.CommonResponse.clear_route_cache>`\n   177→  // field is set in an external processor response.\n   178→  bool disable_clear_route_cache = 11;\n   179→\n   180→  // Allow headers matching the ``forward_rules`` to be forwarded to the external processing server.\n   181→  // If not set, all headers are forwarded to the external processing server.\n   182→  HeaderForwardingRules forward_rules = 12;\n   183→\n   184→  // Additional metadata to be added to the filter state for logging purposes. There will be no\n   200→  // more external processing for this stream from now on.\n   201→  bool disable_immediate_response = 15;\n   202→\n   203→  // Options related to the sending and receiving of dynamic metadata.\n   204→  MetadataOptions metadata_options = 16;\n   205→\n   206→  // If true, send each part of the HTTP request or response specified by ProcessingMode\n   207→  // without pausing on filter chain iteration. It is \"Send and Go\" mode that can be used\n   208→  // by external processor to observe Envoy data and status. In this mode:\n   209→  //\n   210→  // 1. NONE mode(i.e., skip body processing) will still work as expected.\n   212→  //\n   213→  // 2. External processor should not send back processing response, as any responses will be ignored.\n   214→  // This also means that\n   215→  // :ref:`message_timeout <envoy_v3_api_field_extensions.filters.http.ext_proc.v3.ExternalProcessor.message_timeout>`\n   216→  // restriction doesn't apply to this mode.\n   217→  //\n   218→  // 3. External processor may still close the stream to indicate that no more messages are needed.\n   219→  //\n   220→  // .. warning::\n   221→  //\n   222→  //    Flow control is necessary mechanism to prevent the fast sender (either downstream client or upstream server)\n   223→  //    from overwhelming the external processor when its processing speed is slower.\n   224→  //    This protective measure is being explored and developed but has not been ready yet, so please use your own\n   225→  //    discretion when enabling this feature.\n   226→  //    This work is currently tracked under https://github.com/envoyproxy/envoy/issues/33319.\n   227→  //\n   228→  bool observability_mode = 17;\n   229→}\n   230→\n   231→// The MetadataOptions structure defines options for the sending and receiving of\n   232→// dynamic metadata. If ``allowed_headers`` is set, and ``disallowed_headers`` is not set, only headers in\n   266→//      the ``allowed_headers`` are forwarded.\n   267→//   4. External Processing Filter]\n// External Processing Filter\n// [#extension: envoy.filters.http.ext_proc]\n\n// The External Processing filter allows an external service to act on HTTP traffic in a flexible way.\n\n// **Current Implementation Status:**\n// All options and processing modes are implemented except for the following:\n//\n// * \"async mode\" is not implemented.\n\n// The filter communicates with an external gRPC service called an \"external processor\"\n// that can do a variety of things with the request and response:\n//\n// * Access and modify the HTTP headers on the request, response, or both\n// * Access and modify the HTTP request and response bodies\n// * Access and modify the dynamic stream metadata\n// * Immediately send an HTTP response downstream and terminate other processing\n//\n// The filter communicates with the server using a gRPC bidirectional stream. After the initial\n// request, the external server is in control over what additional data is sent to it\n// and how it should be processed.\n//\n// By implementing the protocol specified by the stream, the external server can choose:\n//\n// * Whether it receives the response message at all\n// * Whether it receives the message body at all, in separate chunks, or as a single buffer\n// * Whether subsequent HTTP requests are transmitted synchronously or whether they are\n//   sent asynchronously.\n// * To modify request or response trailers if they already exist\n//\n// The filter supports up to six different processing steps. Each is represented by\n// a gRPC stream message that is sent to the external processor. For each message, the\n// processor must send a matching response.\n//\n// * Request headers: Contains the headers from the original HTTP request.\n// * Request body: Delivered if they are present and sent in a single message if\n//   the BUFFERED or BUFFERED_PARTIAL mode is chosen, in multiple messages if the\n//   STREAMED mode is chosen, and not at all otherwise.\n// * Request trailers: Delivered if they are present and if the trailer mode is set\n//   to SEND.\n// * Response headers: Contains the headers from the HTTP response. Keep in mind\n//   that if the upstream system sends them before processing the request body that\n//   this message may arrive before the complete body.\n// * Response body: Sent according to the processing mode like the request body.\n// * Response trailers: Delivered according to the processing mode like the\n//   request trailers.\n//\n// By default, the processor sends only the request and response headers messages.\n// This may be changed to include any of the six steps by changing the processing_mode\n// setting of the filter configuration, or by setting the mode_override of any response\n// from the external processor. The latter is only enabled if allow_mode_override is\n// set to true. This way, a processor may, for example, use information\n// in the request header to determine whether the message body must be examined, or whether\n// the proxy should simply stream it straight through.\n//\n// All of this together allows a server to process the filter traffic in fairly\n// sophisticated ways. For example:\n//\n// * A server may choose to examine all or part of the HTTP message bodies depending\n//   on the content of the headers.\n// * A server may choose to immediately reject some messages based on their HTTP\n//   headers (or other dynamic metadata) and more carefully examine others.\n// * A server may asynchronously monitor traffic coming through the filter by inspecting\n//   headers, bodies, or both, and then decide to switch to a synchronous processing\n//   mode, either permanently or temporarily.\n//\n// The protocol itself is based on a bidirectional gRPC stream. Envoy will send the\n// server\n// :ref:`ProcessingRequest <envoy_v3_api_msg_service.ext_proc.v3.ProcessingRequest>`\n// messages, and the server must reply with\n// :ref:`ProcessingResponse <envoy_v3_api_msg_service.ext_proc.v3.ProcessingResponse>`.\n//\n// Stats about each gRPC call are recorded in a :ref:`dynamic filter state\n// <arch_overview_advanced_filter_state_sharing>` object in a namespace matching the filter\n// name.\n//\n// [#next-free-field: 18]\nmessage ExternalProcessor {\n  reserved 4;\n\n  reserved \"async_mode\";\n\n  // Configuration for the gRPC service that the filter will communicate with.\n  // The filter supports both the \"Envoy\" and \"Google\" gRPC clients.\n  config.core.v3.GrpcService grpc_service = 1 [(validate.rules).message = {required: true}];\n\n  // By default, if the gRPC stream cannot be established, or if it is closed\n  // prematurely with an error, the filter will fail. Specifically, if the\n  // response headers have not yet been delivered, then it will return a 500\n  // error downstream. If they have been delivered, then instead the HTTP stream to the\n  // downstream client will be reset.\n  // With this parameter set to true, however, then if the gRPC stream is prematurely closed\n  // or could not be opened, processing continues without error.\n  bool failure_mode_allow = 2;\n\n  // Specifies default options for how HTTP headers, trailers, and bodies are\n  // sent. See ProcessingMode for details.\n  ProcessingMode processing_mode = 3;\n\n  // Envoy provides a number of :ref:`attributes <arch_overview_attributes>`\n  // for expressive policies. Each attribute name provided in this field will be\n  // matched against that list and populated in the request_headers message.\n  // See the :ref:`attribute documentation <arch_overview_request_attributes>`\n  // for the list of supported attributes and their types.\n  repeated string request_attributes = 5;\n\n  // Envoy provides a number of :ref:`attributes <arch_overview_attributes>`\n  // for expressive policies. Each attribute name provided in this field will be\n  // matched against that list and populated in the response_headers message.\n  // See the :ref:`attribute documentation <arch_overview_attributes>`\n  // for the list of supported attributes and their types.\n  repeated string response_attributes = 6;\n\n  // Specifies the timeout for each individual message sent on the stream and\n  // when the filter is running in synchronous mode. Whenever the proxy sends\n  // a message on the stream that requires a response, it will reset this timer,\n  // and will stop processing and return an error (subject to the processing mode)\n  // if the timer expires before a matching response is received. There is no\n  // timeout when the filter is running in asynchronous mode. Zero is a valid\n  // config which means the timer will be triggered immediately. If not\n  // configured, default is 200 milliseconds.\n  google.protobuf.Duration message_timeout = 7 [(validate.rules).duration = {\n    lte {seconds: 3600}\n    gte {}\n  }];\n\n  // Optional additional prefix to use when emitting statistics. This allows to distinguish\n  // emitted statistics between configured *ext_proc* filters in an HTTP filter chain.\n  string stat_prefix = 8;\n\n  // Rules that determine what modifications an external processing server may\n  // make to message headers. {"type":"user","message":{"role":"user","content":[{"tool_use_id":"toolu_01Nka3MdXePkqT368ch8rdw3","type":"tool_result","content":"     1→syntax = \"proto3\";\n     2→\n     3→package envoy.extensions.filters.http.ext_proc.v3;\n     4→\n     5→import \"envoy/config/common/mutation_rules/v3/mutation_rules.proto\";\n     6→import \"envoy/config/core/v3/base.proto\";\n     7→import \"udpa/annotations/status.proto\";\n    16→import \"validate/validate.proto\";\n    17→\n    18→option java_package = \"io.envoyproxy.envoy.extensions.filters.http.ext_proc.v3\";\n    19→option java_outer_classname = \"ExtProcProto\";\n    20→option java_multiple_files = true;\n    21→option go_package = \"github.com/envoyproxy/go-control-plane/envoy/extensions/filters/http/ext_proc/v3;ext_procv3\";\n    22→option (udpa.annotations.file_status).package_version_status = ACTIVE;\n    23→\n    24→// [#protodoc-title: External Processing Filter]\n    25→// External Processing Filter\n    26→// [#extension: envoy.filters.http.ext_proc]\n    27→\n    28→// The External Processing filter allows an external service to act on HTTP traffic in a flexible way.\n    29→\n    30→// **Current Implementation Status:**\n    31→// All options and processing modes are implemented except for the following:\n    32→//\n    33→// * \"async mode\" is not implemented.\n    34→\n    35→// The filter communicates with an external gRPC service called an \"external processor\"\n    36→// that can do a variety of things with the request and response:\n    37→//\n    38→// * Access and modify the HTTP headers on the request, response, or both\n    39→// * Access and modify the HTTP request and response bodies\n    40→// * Access and modify the dynamic stream metadata\n    41→// * Immediately send an HTTP response downstream and terminate other processing\n    42→//\n    43→// The filter communicates with the server using a gRPC bidirectional stream. After the initial\n    44→// request, the external server is in control over what additional data is sent to it\n    45→// and how it should be processed.\n    46→//\n    47→// By implementing the protocol specified by the stream, the external server can choose:\n    48→//\n    49→// * Whether it receives the response message at all\n    50→// * Whether it receives the message body at all, in separate chunks, or as a single buffer\n    51→// * Whether subsequent HTTP requests are transmitted synchronously or whether they are\n    52→//   sent asynchronously.\n    53→// * To modify request or response trailers if they already exist\n    54→//\n    55→// The filter supports up to six different processing steps. Each is represented by\n    56→// a gRPC stream message that is sent to the external processor. For each message, the\n    57→// processor must send a matching response.\n    58→//\n    59→// * Request headers: Contains the headers from the original HTTP request.\n    60→// * Request body: Delivered if they are present and sent in a single message if\n    61→//   the BUFFERED or BUFFERED_PARTIAL mode is chosen, in multiple messages if the\n    62→//   STREAMED mode is chosen, and not at all otherwise.\n    63→// * Request trailers: Delivered if they are present and if the trailer mode is set\n    64→//   to SEND.\n    65→// * Response headers: Contains the headers from the HTTP response. Keep in mind\n    66→//   that if the upstream system sends them before processing the request body that\n    67→//   this message may arrive before the complete body.\n    68→// * Response body: Sent according to the processing mode like the request body.\n    69→// * Response trailers: Delivered according to the processing mode like the\n    70→//   request trailers.\n    71→//\n    72→// By default, the processor sends only the request and response headers messages.\n    73→// This may be changed to include any of the six steps by changing the processing_mode\n    74→// setting of the filter configuration, or by setting the mode_override of any response\n    75→// from the external processor. The latter is only enabled if allow_mode_override is\n    76→// set to true. This way, a processor may, for example, use information\n    77→// in the request header to determine whether the message body must be examined, or whether\n    78→// the proxy should simply stream it straight through.\n    79→//\n    80→// All of this together allows a server to process the filter traffic in fairly\n    81→// sophisticated ways. For example:\n    82→//\n    83→// * A server may choose to examine all or part of the HTTP message bodies depending\n    84→//   on the content of the headers.\n    85→// * A server may choose to immediately reject some messages based on their HTTP\n    86→//   headers (or other dynamic metadata) and more carefully examine others.\n    87→// * A server may asynchronously monitor traffic coming through the filter by inspecting\n    88→//   headers, bodies, or both, and then decide to switch to a synchronous processing\n    89→//   mode, either permanently or temporarily.\n    90→//\n    91→// The protocol itself is based on a bidirectional gRPC stream. Envoy will send the\n    92→// server\n    93→// :ref:`ProcessingRequest <envoy_v3_api_msg_service.ext_proc.v3.ProcessingRequest>`\n    94→// messages, and the server must reply with\n    95→// :ref:`ProcessingResponse <envoy_v3_api_msg_service.ext_proc.v3.ProcessingResponse>`.\n    96→//\n    97→// Stats about each gRPC call are recorded in a :ref:`dynamic filter state\n    98→// <arch_overview_advanced_filter_state_sharing>` object in a namespace matching the filter\n    99→// name.\n   100→//\n   101→// [#next-free-field: 20]\n   102→message ExternalProcessor {\n   103→  // Describes the route cache action to be taken when an external processor response\n   104→  // is received in response to request headers.\n   105→  enum RouteCacheAction {\n   106→    // The default behavior is to clear the route cache only when the\n   107→    // :ref:`clear_route_cache <envoy_v3_api_field_service.ext_proc.v3.CommonResponse.clear_route_cache>`\n   108→    // field is set in an external processor response.\n   109→    DEFAULT = 0;\n   110→\n   111→    // Always clear the route cache irrespective of the clear_route_cache bit in\n   112→    // the external processor response.\n   113→    CLEAR = 1;\n   114→\n   115→    // Do not clear the route cache irrespective of the clear_route_cache bit in\n   116→    // the external processor response. Setting to RETAIN is equivalent to set the\n   117→    // :ref:`disable_clear_route_cache <envoy_v3_api_field_extensions.filters.http.ext_proc.v3.ExternalProcessor.disable_clear_route_cache>`\n   118→    // to true.\n   119→    RETAIN = 2;\n   120→  }\n   121→\n   122→  reserved 4;\n   123→\n   124→  reserved \"async_mode\";\n   125→\n   126→  // Configuration for the gRPC service that the filter will communicate with.\n   127→  // The filter supports both the \"Envoy\" and \"Google\" gRPC clients.\n   128→  config.core.v3.GrpcService grpc_service = 1 [(validate.rules).message = {required: true}];\n   129→\n   130→  // By default, if the gRPC stream cannot be established, or if it is closed\n   131→  // prematurely with an error, the filter will fail. ACTIVE;\n\n// [#protodoc-title: External Processing Filter]\n// External Processing Filter\n// [#extension: envoy.filters.http.ext_proc]\n\n// The External Processing filter allows an external service to act on HTTP traffic in a flexible way.\n\n// **Current Implementation Status:**\n// All options and processing modes are implemented except for the following:\n//\n// * \"async mode\" is not implemented.\n\n// The filter communicates with an external gRPC service called an \"external processor\"\n// that can do a variety of things with the request and response:\n//\n// * Access and modify the HTTP headers on the request, response, or both\n// * Access and modify the HTTP request and response bodies\n// * Access and modify the dynamic stream metadata\n// * Immediately send an HTTP response downstream and terminate other processing\n//\n// The filter communicates with the server using a gRPC bidirectional stream. After the initial\n// request, the external server is in control over what additional data is sent to it\n// and how it should be processed.\n//\n// By implementing the protocol specified by the stream, the external server can choose:\n//\n// * Whether it receives the response message at all\n// * Whether it receives the message body at all, in separate chunks, or as a single buffer\n// * Whether subsequent HTTP requests are transmitted synchronously or whether they are\n//   sent asynchronously.\n// * To modify request or response trailers if they already exist\n//\n// The filter supports up to six different processing steps. Each is represented by\n// a gRPC stream message that is sent to the external processor. For each message, the\n// processor must send a matching response.\n//\n// * Request headers: Contains the headers from the original HTTP request.\n// * Request body: Delivered if they are present and sent in a single message if\n//   the BUFFERED or BUFFERED_PARTIAL mode is chosen, in multiple messages if the\n//   STREAMED mode is chosen, and not at all otherwise.\n// * Request trailers: Delivered if they are present and if the trailer mode is set\n//   to SEND.\n// * Response headers: Contains the headers from the HTTP response. Keep in mind\n//   that if the upstream system sends them before processing the request body that\n//   this message may arrive before the complete body.\n// * Response body: Sent according to the processing mode like the request body.\n// * Response trailers: Delivered according to the processing mode like the\n//   request trailers.\n//\n// By default, the processor sends only the request and response headers messages.\n// This may be changed to include any of the six steps by changing the processing_mode\n// setting of the filter configuration, or by setting the mode_override of any response\n// from the external processor. The latter is only enabled if allow_mode_override is\n// set to true. This way, a processor may, for example, use information\n// in the request header to determine whether the message body must be examined, or whether\n// the proxy should simply stream it straight through.\n//\n// All of this together allows a server to process the filter traffic in fairly\n// sophisticated ways. For example:\n//\n// * A server may choose to examine all or part of the HTTP message bodies depending\n//   on the content of the headers.\n// * A server may choose to immediately reject some messages based on their HTTP\n//   headers (or other dynamic metadata) and more carefully examine others.\n// * A server may asynchronously monitor traffic coming through the filter by inspecting\n//   headers, bodies, or both, and then decide to switch to a synchronous processing\n//   mode, either permanently or temporarily.\n//\n// The protocol itself is based on a bidirectional gRPC stream. Envoy will send the\n// server\n// :ref:`ProcessingRequest <envoy_v3_api_msg_service.ext_proc.v3.ProcessingRequest>`\n// messages, and the server must reply with\n// :ref:`ProcessingResponse <envoy_v3_api_msg_service.ext_proc.v3.ProcessingResponse>`.\n//\n// Stats about each gRPC call are recorded in a :ref:`dynamic filter state\n// <arch_overview_advanced_filter_state_sharing>` object in a namespace matching the filter\n// name.\n//\n// [#next-free-field: 20]\nmessage ExternalProcessor {\n  // Describes the route cache action to be taken when an external processor response\n  // is received in response to request headers.\n  enum RouteCacheAction {\n    // The default behavior is to clear the route cache only when the\n    // :ref:`clear_route_cache <envoy_v3_api_field_service.ext_proc.v3.CommonResponse.clear_route_cache>`\n    // field is set in an external processor response.\n    DEFAULT = 0;\n\n    // Always clear the route cache irrespective of the clear_route_cache bit in\n    // the external processor response.\n    CLEAR = 1;\n\n    // Do not clear the route cache irrespective of the clear_route_cache bit in\n    // the external processor response. Setting to RETAIN is equivalent to set the\n    // :ref:`disable_clear_route_cache <envoy_v3_api_field_extensions.filters.http.ext_proc.v3.ExternalProcessor.disable_clear_route_cache>`\n    // to true.\n    RETAIN = 2;\n  }\n\n  reserved 4;\n\n  reserved \"async_mode\";\n\n  // Configuration for the gRPC service that the filter will communicate with.\n  // The filter supports both the \"Envoy\" and \"Google\" gRPC clients.\n  config.core.v3.GrpcService grpc_service = 1 [(validate.rules).message = {required: true}];\n\n  // By default, if the gRPC stream cannot be established, or if it is closed\n  // prematurely with an error, the filter will fail. Specifically, if the\n  // response headers have not yet been delivered, then it will return a 500\n  // error downstream. If they have been delivered, then instead the HTTP stream to the\n  // downstream client will be reset.\n  // With this parameter set to true, however, then if the gRPC stream is prematurely closed\n  // or could not be opened, processing continues without error.\n  bool failure_mode_allow = 2;\n\n  // Specifies default options for how HTTP headers, trailers, and bodies are\n  // sent. See ProcessingMode for details.\n  ProcessingMode processing_mode = 3;\n\n  // Envoy provides a number of :ref:`attributes <arch_overview_attributes>`\n  // for expressive policies. Each attribute name provided in this field will be\n  // matched against that list and populated in the request_headers message.\n  // See the :ref:`attribute documentation <arch_overview_request_attributes>`\n  // for the list of supported attributes and their types.\n  repeated string request_attributes = 5;\n\n  // Envoy provides a number of :ref:`attributes <arch_overview_attributes>`\n  // for expressive policies. Each attribute name provided in this field will be\n  // matched against that list and populated in the response_headers message.\n  // See the :ref:`attribute documentation <arch_overview_attributes>`\n  // for the list of supported attributes and their types.\n  repeated string response_attributes = 6;\n\n  // Specifies the timeout for each individual message sent on the stream and\n  // when the filter is running in synchronous mode. Whenever the proxy sends\n  // a message on the stream that requires a response, it will reset this timer,\n  // and will stop processing and return an error (subject to the processing mode)\n  // if the timer expires before a matching response is received. There is no\n  // timeout when the filter is running in asynchronous mode. Zero is a valid\n  // config which means the timer will be triggered immediately. In such case, no local reply will be sent.\n  // Instead, the stream to the external processor will be closed. There will be no\n  // more external processing for this stream from now on.\n  bool disable_immediate_response = 15;\n\n  // Options related to the sending and receiving of dynamic metadata.\n  MetadataOptions metadata_options = 16;\n\n  // If true, send each part of the HTTP request or response specified by ProcessingMode\n  // without pausing on filter chain iteration. It is \"Send and Go\" mode that can be used\n  // by external processor to observe Envoy data and status. In this mode:\n  //\n  // 1. Only STREAMED body processing mode is supported and any other body processing modes will be\n  // ignored. NONE mode(i.e., skip body processing) will still work as expected.\n  //\n  // 2. External processor should not send back processing response, as any responses will be ignored.\n  // This also means that\n  // :ref:`message_timeout <envoy_v3_api_field_extensions.filters.http.ext_proc.v3.ExternalProcessor.message_timeout>`\n  // restriction doesn't apply to this mode.\n  //\n  // 3. External processor may still close the stream to indicate that no more messages are needed.\n  //\n  // .. warning::\n  //\n  //    Flow control is necessary mechanism to prevent the fast sender (either downstream client or upstream server)\n  //    from overwhelming the external processor when its processing speed is slower.\n  //    This protective measure is being explored and developed but has not been ready yet, so please use your own\n  //    discretion when enabling this feature.\n  //    This work is currently tracked under https://github.com/envoyproxy/envoy/issues/33319.\n  //\n  bool observability_mode = 17;\n\n  // Prevents clearing the route-cache when the\n  // :ref:`clear_route_cache <envoy_v3_api_field_service.ext_proc.v3.CommonResponse.clear_route_cache>`\n  // field is set in an external processor response.\n  // Only one of ``disable_clear_route_cache`` or ``route_cache_action`` can be set.\n  // It is recommended to set ``route_cache_action`` which supersedes ``disable_clear_route_cache``.\n  bool disable_clear_route_cache = 11\n      [(udpa.annotations.field_migrate).oneof_promotion = \"clear_route_cache_type\"];\n\n  // Specifies the action to be taken when an external processor response is\n  // received in response to request headers. In this case, Envoy will eventually timeout the external processor stream according to this time limit.\n  // The default value is 5000 milliseconds (5 seconds) if not specified.\n  google.protobuf.Duration deferred_close_timeout = 19;\n}\n\n// The MetadataOptions structure defines options for the sending and receiving of\n// dynamic metadata. By default, request and response headers are sent,\n    27→    // while trailers are skipped.\n    28→    DEFAULT = 0;\n    29→\n    30→    // Send the header or trailer.\n    31→    SEND = 1;\n    32→\n    33→    // Do not send the header or trailer.\n    34→    SKIP = 2;\n    35→  }\n    36→\n    37→  // Control how the request and response bodies are handled\n    38→  // When body mutation by external processor is enabled, ext_proc filter will always remove\n    39→  // the content length header in three cases below because content length can not be guaranteed\n    40→  // to be set correctly:\n    41→  // 1) STREAMED BodySendMode: header processing completes before body mutation comes back.\n    42→  // 2) BUFFERED_PARTIAL BodySendMode: body is buffered and could be injected in different phases.\n    43→  // 3) BUFFERED BodySendMode + SKIP HeaderSendMode: header processing (e.g., update content-length) is skipped.\n    44→  //\n    45→  // In Envoy's http1 codec implementation, removing content length will enable chunked transfer\n    46→  // encoding whenever feasible. The recipient (either client or server) must be able\n    47→  // to parse and decode the chunked transfer coding.\n    48→  // (see `details in RFC9112 <https://tools.ietf.org/html/rfc9112#section-7.1>`_).\n    49→  //\n    50→  // In BUFFERED BodySendMode + SEND HeaderSendMode, content length header is allowed but it is\n    51→  // external processor's responsibility to set the content length correctly matched to the length\n    52→  // of mutated body. If they don't match, the corresponding body mutation will be rejected and\n    53→  // local reply will be sent with an error message.\n    54→  enum BodySendMode {\n    55→    // Do not send the body at all. This is the default.\n    56→    NONE = 0;\n    57→\n    58→    // Stream the body to the server in pieces as they arrive at the\n    59→    // proxy.\n    60→    STREAMED = 1;\n    61→\n    62→    // Buffer the message body in memory and send the entire body at once.\n    63→    // If the body exceeds the configured buffer limit, then the\n    64→    // downstream system will receive an error.\n    65→    BUFFERED = 2;\n    66→\n    67→    // Buffer the message body in memory and send the entire body in one\n    68→    // chunk. If the body exceeds the configured buffer limit, then the body contents\n    69→    // up to the buffer limit will be sent.\n    70→    BUFFERED_PARTIAL = 3;\n    71→  }\n    72→\n    73→  // How to handle the request header. Default is \"SEND\".\n    74→  HeaderSendMode request_header_mode = 1 [(validate.rules).enum = {defined_only: true}];\n    75→\n    76→  // How to handle the response header. Default is \"SEND\".\n    77→  HeaderSendMode response_header_mode = 2 [(validate.rules).enum = {defined_only: true}];\n    78→\n    79→  // How to handle the request body. Default is \"NONE\".\n    80→  BodySendMode request_body_mode = 3 [(validate.rules).enum = {defined_only: true}];\n    81→\n    82→  // How do handle the response body. Default is \"NONE\".\n    83→  BodySendMode response_body_mode = 4 [(validate.rules).enum = {defined_only: true}];\n    84→\n    85→  // How to handle the request trailers. Default is \"SKIP\".\n    86→  HeaderSendMode request_trailer_mode = 5 [(validate.rules).enum = {defined_only: true}];\n    87→\n    88→  // How to handle the response trailers. The processing service itself implements a gRPC interface that allows\nit to respond to events in the lifecycle of an HTTP request / response by examining\nand modifying the headers, body, and trailers of each message, or by returning a brand-new response.\n\nThe protocol itself is based on a bidirectional gRPC stream. Envoy will send the\nexternal processor\n:ref:`ProcessingRequest <envoy_v3_api_msg_service.ext_proc.v3.ProcessingRequest>`\nmessages, and the processor must reply with\n:ref:`ProcessingResponse <envoy_v3_api_msg_service.ext_proc.v3.ProcessingResponse>`\nmessages.\n\nConfiguration options are provided to control which events are sent to the processor.\nThis way, the processor may receive headers, body, and trailers for both\nrequest and response in any combination. The processor may also change this configuration\non a message-by-message basis. This allows for the construction of sophisticated processors\nthat decide how to respond to each message individually to eliminate unnecessary\nstream requests from the proxy.\n\nThis filter is a work in progress. Most of the major bits of functionality\nare complete. The updated list of supported features and implementation status may\nbe found on the :ref:`reference page <envoy_v3_api_msg_extensions.filters.http.ext_proc.v3.ExternalProcessor>`.\n\nStatistics\n----------\nThis filter outputs statistics in the\n``http.<stat_prefix>.ext_proc.`` namespace. The :ref:`stat prefix\n<envoy_v3_api_field_extensions.filters.network.http_connection_manager.v3.HttpConnectionManager.stat_prefix>`\ncomes from the owning HTTP connection manager.\n\nThe following statistics are supported:\n\n.. csv-table::\n  :header: Name, Type, Description\n  :widths: auto\n\n  streams_started, Counter, The number of gRPC streams that have been started to send to the external processing service\n  streams_msgs_sent, Counter, The number of messages sent on those streams\n  streams_msgs_received, Counter, The number of messages received on those streams\n  spurious_msgs_received, Counter, The number of unexpected messages received that violated the protocol\n  streams_closed, Counter, The number of streams successfully closed on either end\n  streams_failed, Counter, The number of times a stream produced a gRPC error\n  failure_mode_allowed, Counter, The number of times an error was ignored due to configuration\n  message_timeouts, Counter, The number of times a message failed to receive a response within the configured timeout\n  rejected_header_mutations, Counter, The number of rejected header mutations\n  clear_route_cache_ignored, Counter, The number of clear cache request that were ignored\n  clear_route_cache_disabled, Counter, The number of clear cache requests that were rejected from being disabled\n","numLines":55,"startLine":1,"totalLines":55}}}

The processing service itself implements a gRPC interface that allows\nit to respond to events in the lifecycle of an HTTP request / response by examining\nand modifying the headers, body, and trailers of each message, or by returning a brand-new response.\n\nThe protocol itself is based on a bidirectional gRPC stream. Envoy will send the\nexternal processor\n:ref:`ProcessingRequest <envoy_v3_api_msg_service.ext_proc.v3.ProcessingRequest>`\nmessages, and the processor must reply with\n:ref:`ProcessingResponse <envoy_v3_api_msg_service.ext_proc.v3.ProcessingResponse>`\nmessages.\n\nConfiguration options are provided to control which events are sent to the processor.\nThis way, the processor may receive headers, body, and trailers for both\nrequest and response in any combination. The processor may also change this configuration\non a message-by-message basis. This allows for the construction of sophisticated processors\nthat decide how to respond to each message individually to eliminate unnecessary\nstream requests from the proxy.\n\nThis filter is a work in progress. Most of the major bits of functionality\nare complete. The updated list of supported features and implementation status may\nbe found on the :ref:`reference page <envoy_v3_api_msg_extensions.filters.http.ext_proc.v3.ExternalProcessor>`.\n\nStatistics\n----------\nThis filter outputs statistics in the\n``http.<stat_prefix>.ext_proc.`` namespace. The :ref:`stat prefix\n<envoy_v3_api_field_extensions.filters.network.http_connection_manager.v3.HttpConnectionManager.stat_prefix>`\ncomes from the owning HTTP connection manager.\n\nThe following statistics are supported:\n\n.. csv-table::\n  :header: Name, Type, Description\n  :widths: auto\n\n  streams_started, Counter, The number of gRPC streams that have been started to send to the external processing service\n  streams_msgs_sent, Counter, The number of messages sent on those streams\n  streams_msgs_received, Counter, The number of messages received on those streams\n  spurious_msgs_received, Counter, The number of unexpected messages received that violated the protocol\n  streams_closed, Counter, The number of streams successfully closed on either end\n  streams_failed, Counter, The number of times a stream produced a gRPC error\n  failure_mode_allowed, Counter, The number of times an error was ignored due to configuration\n  message_timeouts, Counter, The number of times a message failed to receive a response within the configured timeout\n  rejected_header_mutations, Counter, The number of rejected header mutations\n  clear_route_cache_ignored, Counter, The number of clear cache request that were ignored\n  clear_route_cache_disabled, Counter, The number of clear cache requests that were rejected from being disabled\n","numLines":55,"startLine":1,"totalLines":55}}}

Overview\n\nThis migration guide covers upgrading the Envoy External Processing HTTP filter from **v1.30.0 (April 2024)** to **v1.31.0 (July 2024)**. While this is a minor version update, it introduces important new features and refactors the route cache clearing mechanism.\n\n### Key Changes Summary\n\n| Category | Count | Impact |\n|----------|-------|--------|\n| Breaking Changes | 0 (strict) | Low |\n| Deprecated Fields | 1 | Medium |\n| New Features | 3 | Medium |\n| Behavioral Changes | 2 | Medium |\n\n---\n\n## 2. Breaking Changes\n\n### 2.1 No Strict Breaking Changes\n\n**Status:** ✅ Configurations from v1.30 will continue to work in v1.31\n\nThe ext_proc filter maintains backward compatibility - all v1.30 configurations will load and function in v1.31. However, there are important behavioral changes and deprecated fields that warrant attention.\n\n---\n\n## 3. Deprecated Features\n\n### 3.1 `disable_clear_route_cache` Field Deprecation\n\n**Deprecated Field:** `disable_clear_route_cache` (field 11)\n**Replacement:** `route_cache_action` (field 18)\n**Status:** Will be marked for removal in a future version\n**Motivation:** Provides more granular control over route cache behavior beyond simple enable/disable\n\n#### Details\n\nThe `disable_clear_route_cache` boolean field is now superseded by the more flexible `route_cache_action` enum. While the old field continues to work, the new field offers three distinct behaviors:\n\n**Proto Definition Change:**\n\n**v1.30.0:**\n```protobuf\n// api/envoy/extensions/filters/http/ext_proc/v3/ext_proc.proto\n\nmessage ExternalProcessor {\n  // ...\n\n  // Prevents clearing the route-cache when the\n  // clear_route_cache field is set in an external processor response.\n  bool disable_clear_route_cache = 11;\n}\n```\n\n**v1.31.0:**\n```protobuf\n// api/envoy/extensions/filters/http/ext_proc/v3/ext_proc.proto\n\nmessage ExternalProcessor {\n  enum RouteCacheAction {\n    // The default behavior is to clear the route cache only when the\n    // clear_route_cache field is set in an external processor response.\n    DEFAULT = 0;\n\n    // Always clear the route cache irrespective of the clear_route_cache bit in\n    // the external processor response.\n    CLEAR = 1;\n\n    // Do not clear the route cache irrespective of the clear_route_cache bit in\n    // the external processor response. Setting to RETAIN is equivalent to set the\n    // disable_clear_route_cache to true.\n    RETAIN = 2;\n  }\n\n  // Prevents clearing the route-cache when the\n  // clear_route_cache field is set in an external processor response.\n  // Only one of ``disable_clear_route_cache`` or ``route_cache_action`` can be set.\n  // It is recommended to set ``route_cache_action`` which supersedes ``disable_clear_route_cache``.\n  bool disable_clear_route_cache = 11\n      [(udpa.annotations.field_migrate).oneof_promotion = \"clear_route_cache_type\"];\n\n  // Specifies the action to be taken when an external processor response is\n  // received in response to request headers. It is recommended to set this field than set\n  // disable_clear_route_cache.\n  // Only one of ``disable_clear_route_cache`` or ``route_cache_action`` can be set.\n  RouteCacheAction route_cache_action = 18\n      [(udpa.annotations.field_migrate).oneof_promotion = \"clear_route_cache_type\"];\n}\n```\n\n#### Migration Steps\n\n**Option 1: Using `disable_clear_route_cache` (Current v1.30 Config)**\n```yaml\n# v1.30.0 configuration\nadmin:\n  address:\n    socket_address:\n      address: 127.0.0.1\n      port_value: 9901\n\nstatic_resources:\n  listeners:\n  - name: listener_0\n    address:\n      socket_address:\n        address: 0.0.0.0\n        port_value: 10000\n    filter_chains:\n    - filters:\n      - name: envoy.filters.network.http_connection_manager\n        typed_config:\n          \"@type\": type.googleapis.com/envoy.extensions.filters.network.http_connection_manager.v3.HttpConnectionManager\n          stat_prefix: ingress_http\n          http_filters:\n          - name: envoy.filters.http.ext_proc\n            typed_config:\n              \"@type\": type.googleapis.com/envoy.extensions.filters.http.ext_proc.v3.ExternalProcessor\n              grpc_service:\n                envoy_grpc:\n                  cluster_name: ext_proc_cluster\n              disable_clear_route_cache: true  # ⚠️ DEPRECATED in v1.31.0\n              processing_mode:\n                request_header_mode: SEND\n                response_header_mode: SEND\n```\n\n**Option 2: Using `route_cache_action` (Recommended v1.31.0 Config)**\n```yaml\n# v1.31.0 configuration - RECOMMENDED\nadmin:\n  address:\n    socket_address:\n      address: 127.0.0.1\n      port_value: 9901\n\nstatic_resources:\n  listeners:\n  - name: listener_0\n    address:\n      socket_address:\n        address: 0.0.0.0\n        port_value: 10000\n    filter_chains:\n    - filters:\n      - name: envoy.filters.network.http_connection_manager\n        typed_config:\n          \"@type\": type.googleapis.com/envoy.extensions.filters.network.http_connection_manager.v3.HttpConnectionManager\n          stat_prefix: ingress_http\n          http_filters:\n          - name: envoy.filters.http.ext_proc\n            typed_config:\n              \"@type\": type.googleapis.com/envoy.extensions.filters.http.ext_proc.v3.ExternalProcessor\n              grpc_service:\n                envoy_grpc:\n                  cluster_name: ext_proc_cluster\n              route_cache_action: RETAIN  # ✅ RECOMMENDED in v1.31.0\n              processing_mode:\n                request_header_mode: SEND\n                response_header_mode: SEND\n```\n\n#### Mapping Table\n\n| v1.30.0 Config | v1.31.0 Equivalent | Behavior |\n|----------------|-------------------|----------|\n| `disable_clear_route_cache: false` (default) | `route_cache_action: DEFAULT` | Clear cache only when ext_proc response requests it |\n| `disable_clear_route_cache: true` | `route_cache_action: RETAIN` | Never clear cache, regardless of ext_proc response |\n| — | `route_cache_action: CLEAR` | Always clear cache, regardless of ext_proc response |\n\n#### Validation Error\n\nIn v1.31.0, attempting to set both `disable_clear_route_cache` and `route_cache_action` to non-default values will result in a validation error:\n\n```\nEnvoyException: disable_clear_route_cache and route_cache_action can not be set to none-default at the same time.\n```\n\n**Implementation Reference:**\n`source/extensions/filters/http/ext_proc/ext_proc.cc:213-221`\n\n---\n\n## 4. New Features\n\n### 4.1 Observability Mode\n\n**Field:** `observability_mode` (field 17)\n**Type:** `bool`\n**Default:** `false`\n**Availability:** v1.31.0+\n**Status:** ✅ Fully Implemented\n\n#### Purpose\n\nObservability mode enables a \"send and go\" pattern where the ext_proc filter sends HTTP request/response data to the external processor **without waiting for responses**. This allows external processors to observe and analyze traffic without blocking the HTTP stream processing.\n\n#### Key Characteristics\n\n1. **Non-blocking:** Requests are sent asynchronously; responses are ignored\n2. **Streaming only:** Body processing mode is restricted to STREAMED or NONE\n3. **Stream closure:** External processor can close the stream to stop receiving data\n4. **No flow control:** Currently relies on external processor to handle backpressure\n5. **Deferred closure:** Streams are closed after a configurable timeout to prevent resource leaks\n\n#### Use Cases\n\n- **Monitoring and analytics:** Track all traffic patterns without affecting request processing\n- **Real-time logging:** Send detailed request/response information for downstream analysis\n- **Threat detection:** Analyze traffic for security anomalies without latency impact\n- **Compliance auditing:** Record all traffic for compliance requirements\n\n#### Configuration Example\n\n```yaml\nstatic_resources:\n  listeners:\n  - name: listener_0\n    address:\n      socket_address:\n        address: 0.0.0.0\n        port_value: 10000\n    filter_chains:\n    - filters:\n      - name: envoy.filters.network.http_connection_manager\n        typed_config:\n          \"@type\": type.googleapis.com/envoy.extensions.filters.network.http_connection_manager.v3.HttpConnectionManager\n          stat_prefix: ingress_http\n          http_filters:\n          - name: envoy.filters.http.ext_proc\n            typed_config:\n              \"@type\": type.googleapis.com/envoy.extensions.filters.http.ext_proc.v3.ExternalProcessor\n              grpc_service:\n                envoy_grpc:\n                  cluster_name: ext_proc_cluster\n              observability_mode: true  # ✅ NEW in v1.31.0\n              processing_mode:\n                request_header_mode: SEND\n                response_header_mode: SEND\n                request_body_mode: STREAMED   # Only STREAMED or NONE allowed\n                response_body_mode: STREAMED  # Only STREAMED or NONE allowed\n              deferred_close_timeout: 5s  # Optional: timeout for stream closure\n```\n\n#### Behavioral Differences\n\n| Aspect | Normal Mode | Observability Mode |\n|--------|------------|-------------------|\n| Response Handling | Blocks processing, waits for response | Ignores responses |\n| Message Timeout | Enforced | Not enforced |\n| Body Modes | NONE, STREAMED, BUFFERED, BUFFERED_PARTIAL | STREAMED or NONE |\n| Stream Closure | Automatic | Deferred (configurable timeout) |\n| Use Case | Active modification/rejection | Passive observation |\n| Performance Impact | Adds latency | Minimal (fire-and-forget) |\n\n#### Implementation Details\n\n- **Header File:** `source/extensions/filters/http/ext_proc/ext_proc.h:212`\n- **Implementation:** `source/extensions/filters/http/ext_proc/ext_proc.cc:186, 405-408`\n- **New Methods:**\n  - `sendHeadersInObservabilityMode()` - sends headers without waiting\n  - `sendDataInObservabilityMode()` - sends body data without waiting\n  - `deferredCloseStream()` - closes stream after timeout\n\n### 4.2 Route Cache Action Enum\n\n**Field:** `route_cache_action` (field 18)\n**Type:** `enum RouteCacheAction`\n**Default:** `DEFAULT`\n**Availability:** v1.31.0+\n**Status:** ✅ Fully Implemented\n\n#### Purpose\n\nProvides explicit control over Envoy's route cache behavior when receiving responses from the external processor. This is more flexible than the boolean `disable_clear_route_cache` field.\n\n#### Enum Values\n\n```protobuf\nenum RouteCacheAction {\n  // The default behavior is to clear the route cache only when the\n  // clear_route_cache field is set in an external processor response.\n  DEFAULT = 0;\n\n  // Always clear the route cache irrespective of the clear_route_cache bit in\n  // the external processor response.\n  CLEAR = 1;\n\n  // Do not clear the route cache irrespective of the clear_route_cache bit in\n  // the external processor response.\n  RETAIN = 2;\n}\n```\n\n#### Decision Matrix\n\n| Scenario | DEFAULT | CLEAR | RETAIN |\n|----------|---------|-------|--------|\n| Ext_proc sets `clear_route_cache: true` | Cache cleared | Cache cleared | Cache NOT cleared |\n| Ext_proc sets `clear_route_cache: false` | Cache NOT cleared | Cache cleared | Cache NOT cleared |\n| Ext_proc doesn't set field | Cache NOT cleared | Cache cleared | Cache NOT cleared |\n\n#### Configuration Examples\n\n**Scenario 1: External processor controls cache clearing (DEFAULT)**\n```yaml\nroute_cache_action: DEFAULT  # Respect ext_proc decisions\n```\n\n**Scenario 2: Always refresh route on header modification (CLEAR)**\n```yaml\nroute_cache_action: CLEAR  # Always clear to ensure fresh routing decision\n# Use when external processor might modify request headers that affect routing\n```\n\n**Scenario 3: Never clear cache (RETAIN)**\n```yaml\nroute_cache_action: RETAIN  # Never clear, improve performance\n# Use when external processor only modifies non-routing headers\n```\n\n#### Implementation Reference\n\n- **Proto Definition:** `api/envoy/extensions/filters/http/ext_proc/v3/ext_proc.proto:105-120`\n- **Header File:** `source/extensions/filters/http/ext_proc/ext_proc.h:232-235`\n- **Implementation:** `source/extensions/filters/http/ext_proc/ext_proc.cc:187`\n\n### 4.3 Deferred Close Timeout\n\n**Field:** `deferred_close_timeout` (field 19)\n**Type:** `google.protobuf.Duration`\n**Default:** `5000ms` (5 seconds)\n**Availability:** v1.31.0+\n**Status:** ✅ Fully Implemented\n**Prerequisites:** Only applies when `observability_mode: true`\n\n#### Purpose\n\nControls how long gRPC streams to the external processor remain open in observability mode. This prevents streams from being held indefinitely while still allowing the external processor time to process outstanding messages.\n\n#### Configuration Example\n\n```yaml\nstatic_resources:\n  listeners:\n  - name: listener_0\n    address:\n      socket_address:\n        address: 0.0.0.0\n        port_value: 10000\n    filter_chains:\n    - filters:\n      - name: envoy.filters.network.http_connection_manager\n        typed_config:\n          \"@type\": type.googleapis.com/envoy.extensions.filters.network.http_connection_manager.v3.HttpConnectionManager\n          stat_prefix: ingress_http\n          http_filters:\n          - name: envoy.filters.http.ext_proc\n            typed_config:\n              \"@type\": type.googleapis.com/envoy.extensions.filters.http.ext_proc.v3.ExternalProcessor\n              grpc_service:\n                envoy_grpc:\n                  cluster_name: ext_proc_cluster\n              observability_mode: true\n              processing_mode:\n                request_header_mode: SEND\n                response_header_mode: SEND\n              deferred_close_timeout: 10s  # Wait up to 10 seconds before closing stream\n```\n\n#### Default Behavior\n\nIf not specified, Envoy uses **5 seconds** (defined in code as `DEFAULT_DEFERRED_CLOSE_TIMEOUT_MS`).\n\n#### Tuning Recommendations\n\n| Scenario | Recommended Timeout | Reason |\n|----------|-------------------|--------|\n| Low-latency observation | 2-3s | Minimize resource usage |\n| Standard observation | 5s (default) | Balanced approach |\n| High-volume streaming | 10-15s | Allow time for processing bursts |\n| Batch processing | 30s+ | External processor batches and processes offline |\n\n#### Implementation Details\n\n- **Constant:** `source/extensions/filters/http/ext_proc/ext_proc.h:150`\n- **Initialization:** `source/extensions/filters/http/ext_proc/ext_proc.cc:188-189, 212-223`\n- **Stream Management:** `ThreadLocalStreamManager`, `DeferredDeletableStream` classes\n\n---\n\n## 5. Migration Steps\n\n### 5.1 Pre-Migration Checklist\n\n- [ ] Review current ext_proc configuration for deprecated fields\n- [ ] Audit external processor implementations for compatibility\n- [ ] Plan testing strategy for new features\n- [ ] Review metrics and logging for troubleshooting\n- [ ] Prepare rollback plan\n\n### 5.2 Step-by-Step Migration\n\n#### Step 1: Update Envoy Binary\n\n```bash\n# Backup current version\ncp /path/to/envoy /path/to/envoy-v1.30.bak\n\n# Install v1.31.0\n# Download or build Envoy v1.31.0\n# Verify binary: ./envoy --version\n```\n\n#### Step 2: Update Configuration Files\n\n**If using `disable_clear_route_cache`:**\n\n```bash\n# Find all configurations using the deprecated field\ngrep -r \"disable_clear_route_cache\" /etc/envoy/\n\n# Update each configuration\n# OLD:\n# disable_clear_route_cache: true\n\n# NEW:\n# route_cache_action: RETAIN\n```\n\n**Example migration script:**\n```bash\n#!/bin/bash\nfind /etc/envoy -name \"*.yaml\" -type f | while read file; do\n  if grep -q \"disable_clear_route_cache: true\" \"$file\"; then\n    sed -i 's/disable_clear_route_cache: true/route_cache_action: RETAIN/g' \"$file\"\n    echo \"Updated: $file\"\n  fi\ndone\n```\n\n#### Step 3: Validate Configuration\n\n```bash\n# Verify configuration syntax\n./envoy -c /etc/envoy/envoy.yaml --mode validate\n\n# Expected output:\n# configuration OK\n```\n\n#### Step 4: Test with Canary Deployment\n\n```bash\n# Deploy to canary environment with v1.31.0\n# Run integration tests\n# Monitor metrics:\n#   - ext_proc.streams_started\n#   - ext_proc.stream_msgs_sent\n#   - ext_proc.stream_msgs_received\n#   - ext_proc.message_timeouts\n#   - ext_proc.clear_route_cache_*\n```\n\n#### Step 5: Evaluate New Features\n\n**If interested in observability mode:**\n\n1. Deploy experimental configuration with `observability_mode: true`\n2. Monitor external processor resource usage\n3. Verify message delivery and stream closure behavior\n4. Adjust `deferred_close_timeout` based on observations\n\n#### Step 6: Production Rollout\n\n```bash\n# Rolling update strategy\n# 1. Update control plane configuration\n# 2. Rolling restart of Envoy instances (e.g., 25% at a time)\n# 3. Monitor for errors and performance changes\n# 4. Complete rollout when no issues detected\n```\n\n### 5.3 Validation Checklist\n\nAfter upgrading to v1.31.0:\n\n- [ ] Configuration loads without errors\n- [ ] No validation errors for ext_proc filter\n- [ ] External processor gRPC connectivity established\n- [ ] Metrics show normal request flow\n- [ ] No unexpected error rates\n- [ ] Route cache clearing behavior as expected\n- [ ] (If using observability_mode) Streams open/close normally\n\n---\n\n## 6. Behavioral Changes\n\n### 6.1 External Processor Timeout Response Code\n\n**Change:** Timeout handling now returns `504 Gateway Timeout`\n**Status:** ✅ Implemented in v1.31.0\n**Scope:** Applies when external processor doesn't respond within `message_timeout`\n\n#### Impact\n\n**v1.30.0 Behavior:**\n- Timeout errors might result in `500 Internal Server Error` or stream reset\n- Inconsistent behavior depending on filter state\n\n**v1.31.0 Behavior:**\n- Timeout errors consistently return `504 Gateway Timeout` to downstream client\n- More semantically correct (indicates upstream, not proxy)\n- Easier to identify external processor issues in metrics\n\n#### Example\n\n```\nClient Request → Envoy → Ext_proc Timeout\n↓\nEnvoy returns: 504 Gateway Timeout\nReason: External processor did not respond within message_timeout\n```\n\n### 6.2 Route Cache Action Default Behavior\n\n**Change:** Replaces implicit behavior with explicit enum\n**Status:** ✅ Implemented in v1.31.0\n**Scope:** Route cache clearing decision-making\n\n#### Impact\n\n**v1.30.0:**\n- Boolean flag (`disable_clear_route_cache: true/false`)\n- Limited to two states\n\n**v1.31.0:**\n- Enum with three explicit states\n- More expressive control over caching behavior\n- Better performance optimization possibilities\n\n---\n\n## 7. Testing Recommendations\n\n### 8.1 Unit Testing\n\n```bash\n# Run ext_proc filter unit tests\nbazel test //test/extensions/filters/http/ext_proc:...\n\n# Verify specific test categories\nbazel test //test/extensions/filters/http/ext_proc:ext_proc_filter_test\nbazel test //test/extensions/filters/http/ext_proc:ext_proc_integration_test\n```\n\n### 8.2 Integration Testing Strategy\n\n#### Test Case 1: Basic Functionality\n```\nObjective: Verify ext_proc filter processes headers correctly\nSteps:\n  1. Send HTTP request with custom headers\n  2. External processor modifies headers\n  3. Verify downstream receives modified headers\n  4. Verify response headers processed correctly\nExpected: All headers modified as expected, no errors\n```\n\n#### Test Case 2: Route Cache Action Behavior\n```\nObjective: Verify route_cache_action enum works correctly\nSteps:\n  1. Configure route_cache_action: DEFAULT\n  2. Modify request headers that affect routing\n  3. Verify route is re-evaluated (cache cleared)\n  4. Repeat with route_cache_action: RETAIN\n  5. Verify old route is still used (cache not cleared)\nExpected: Route caching behavior matches configuration\n```\n\n#### Test Case 3: Observability Mode\n```\nObjective: Verify observability_mode sends data without blocking\nSteps:\n  1. Enable observability_mode: true\n  2. Configure external processor to be slow (5s response time)\n  3. Send HTTP requests\n  4. Verify requests complete within normal time (not blocked)\n  5. Verify external processor eventually receives data\nExpected: Requests complete quickly, external processor receives data asynchronously\n```\n\n#### Test Case 4: Deferred Close Timeout\n```\nObjective: Verify deferred_close_timeout controls stream closure\nSteps:\n  1. Enable observability_mode: true\n  2. Set deferred_close_timeout: 2s\n  3. Send HTTP request\n  4. Monitor gRPC stream lifecycle\n  5. Verify stream closes approximately after 2 seconds\nExpected: Stream closes after configured timeout\n```\n\n#### Test Case 5: Timeout Handling\n```\nObjective: Verify external processor timeouts return 504\nSteps:\n  1. Configure external processor with slow response\n  2. Set message_timeout: 100ms\n  3. Send HTTP request\n  4. Verify response code is 504 Gateway Timeout\nExpected: 504 Gateway Timeout returned on timeout\n```\n\n### 8.3 Metrics Verification\n\nMonitor these metrics during testing:\n\n```bash\n# Count of streams started\nenvoy_http_ext_proc_streams_started\n\n# Count of messages sent to external processor\nenvoy_http_ext_proc_stream_msgs_sent\n\n# Count of messages received from external processor\nenvoy_http_ext_proc_stream_msgs_received\n\n# Count of message timeouts\nenvoy_http_ext_proc_message_timeouts\n\n# Count of clear_route_cache operations\nenvoy_http_ext_proc_clear_route_cache_*\n\n# Breakdown by route_cache_action behavior\nenvoy_http_ext_proc_clear_route_cache_ignored  # DEFAULT action, not requested\nenvoy_http_ext_proc_clear_route_cache_disabled # RETAIN action, forced ignore\n```\n\n### 8.4 Load Testing\n\n```bash\n# Use wrk or similar tool to generate load\nwrk -t4 -c100 -d30s http://localhost:10000/\n\n# Monitor metrics during load:\n# - Verify latency increase is minimal (observability_mode)\n# - Verify no message loss\n# - Verify streams are properly managed\n# - Check for resource leaks (memory, file descriptors)\n```\n\n---\n\n## 9. Rollback Guidance\n\n### 9.1 Quick Rollback Procedure\n\nIf issues occur after upgrading to v1.31.0:\n\n```bash\n# 1. Revert binary\ncp /path/to/envoy-v1.30.bak /path/to/envoy\n\n# 2. Restore previous configuration\ngit checkout previous_config.yaml\n\n# 3. Restart Envoy\nsystemctl restart envoy\n\n# 4. Verify connectivity\ncurl -i http://localhost:10000/\n\n# 5. Monitor metrics to confirm stability\n```\n\n### 9.2 Configuration Rollback\n\nIf new features are causing issues:\n\n**From v1.31 with observability_mode:**\n```yaml\n# BEFORE (problematic)\nobservability_mode: true\ndeferred_close_timeout: 5s\n\n# AFTER (rollback)\nobservability_mode: false\n# Remove deferred_close_timeout or leave as default\n```\n\n**From v1.31 with route_cache_action:**\n```yaml\n# BEFORE (problematic)\nroute_cache_action: CLEAR\n\n# AFTER (rollback)\nroute_cache_action: DEFAULT\n```\n\n### 9.3 Issue Detection\n\nWatch for these signs that rollback may be needed:\n\n- [ ] High rate of gRPC errors to external processor\n- [ ] Increased message timeout errors\n- [ ] Unexpected route caching behavior\n- [ ] High latency on requests (if observability_mode not used)\n- [ ] Stream connection issues\n- [ ] Configuration validation failures\n\n---\n\n## 10. Common Migration Pitfalls\n\n### 10.1 Pitfall #1: Mixing `disable_clear_route_cache` and `route_cache_action`\n\n**Problem:**\n```yaml\ndisable_clear_route_cache: true\nroute_cache_action: CLEAR\n```\n\n**Error:**\n```\nEnvoyException: disable_clear_route_cache and route_cache_action can not be set to none-default at the same time.\n```\n\n**Solution:** Use only `route_cache_action` in v1.31.0:\n```yaml\nroute_cache_action: RETAIN  # Don't disable, use explicit action\n```\n\n### 10.2 Pitfall #2: Observability Mode with Body Buffering\n\n**Problem:**\n```yaml\nobservability_mode: true\nprocessing_mode:\n  request_body_mode: BUFFERED  # Only STREAMED or NONE allowed\n```\n\n**Behavior:** BUFFERED body mode will be ignored, downgraded to NONE\n\n**Solution:** Only use STREAMED or NONE with observability_mode:\n```yaml\nobservability_mode: true\nprocessing_mode:\n  request_body_mode: STREAMED  # Correct for observability mode\n```\n\n### 10.3 Pitfall #3: Expecting Responses in Observability Mode\n\n**Problem:**\nExternal processor waits for `ProcessingResponse` but Envoy ignores all responses\n\n**Solution:** In observability mode:\n- External processor should NOT expect to receive responses\n- External processor should only observe and consume messages\n- External processor can close the stream to stop receiving data\n\n### 10.4 Pitfall #4: Not Accounting for Deferred Close Timeout\n\n**Problem:**\nExternal processor still processing messages after stream appears closed\n\n**Solution:** Configure appropriate `deferred_close_timeout`:\n```yaml\nobservability_mode: true\ndeferred_close_timeout: 10s  # Increase if processor is slow\n```\n\n### 10.5 Pitfall #5: Timeout Changes in Error Handling\n\n**Problem:**\nMonitoring rules looking for `500 Internal Server Error` miss new `504 Gateway Timeout` responses\n\n**Solution:** Update monitoring and alerting rules:\n```\n# OLD rule\nalert_if(status_code == 500 AND ext_proc_error)\n\n# NEW rule\nalert_if(status_code == 504 AND timeout AND ext_proc_error)\n```\n\n---\n\n## 11. API Reference\n\n### 11.1 ExternalProcessor Message\n\n#### v1.30.0 Schema\n```protobuf\nmessage ExternalProcessor {\n  config.core.v3.GrpcService grpc_service = 1;\n  bool failure_mode_allow = 2;\n  ProcessingMode processing_mode = 3;\n  repeated string request_attributes = 5;\n  repeated string response_attributes = 6;\n  google.protobuf.Duration message_timeout = 7;\n  string stat_prefix = 8;\n  HeaderMutationRules mutation_rules = 9;\n  google.protobuf.Duration max_message_timeout = 10;\n  bool disable_clear_route_cache = 11;\n  HeaderForwardingRules forward_rules = 12;\n  google.protobuf.Struct filter_metadata = 13;\n  bool allow_mode_override = 14;\n  bool disable_immediate_response = 15;\n  MetadataOptions metadata_options = 16;\n  bool observability_mode = 17;\n\n  // [#next-free-field: 18]\n}\n```\n\n#### v1.31.0 Schema\n```protobuf\nmessage ExternalProcessor {\n  enum RouteCacheAction {\n    DEFAULT = 0;\n    CLEAR = 1;\n    RETAIN = 2;\n  }\n\n  config.core.v3.GrpcService grpc_service = 1;\n  bool failure_mode_allow = 2;\n  ProcessingMode processing_mode = 3;\n  repeated string request_attributes = 5;\n  repeated string response_attributes = 6;\n  google.protobuf.Duration message_timeout = 7;\n  string stat_prefix = 8;\n  HeaderMutationRules mutation_rules = 9;\n  google.protobuf.Duration max_message_timeout = 10;\n  bool disable_clear_route_cache = 11 [deprecated];\n  HeaderForwardingRules forward_rules = 12;\n  google.protobuf.Struct filter_metadata = 13;\n  bool allow_mode_override = 14;\n  bool disable_immediate_response = 15;\n  MetadataOptions metadata_options = 16;\n  bool observability_mode = 17;\n  RouteCacheAction route_cache_action = 18;  // NEW\n  google.protobuf.Duration deferred_close_timeout = 19;  // NEW\n\n  // [#next-free-field: 20]\n}\n```\n\n### 11.2 Field Descriptions\n\n| Field | Type | v1.30 | v1.31 | Description |\n|-------|------|-------|-------|-------------|\n| grpc_service | GrpcService | ✅ | ✅ | External processor gRPC service config |\n| failure_mode_allow | bool | ✅ | ✅ | Allow failure without error |\n| processing_mode | ProcessingMode | ✅ | ✅ | Which parts of request/response to send |\n| request_attributes | []string | ✅ | ✅ | Request attributes to include |\n| response_attributes | []string | ✅ | ✅ | Response attributes to include |\n| message_timeout | Duration | ✅ | ✅ | Max time to wait for response |\n| stat_prefix | string | ✅ | ✅ | Metrics prefix |\n| mutation_rules | HeaderMutationRules | ✅ | ✅ | Header modification rules |\n| max_message_timeout | Duration | ✅ | ✅ | Max override_message_timeout allowed |\n| disable_clear_route_cache | bool | ✅ | ⚠️ Deprecated | Never clear route cache |\n| forward_rules | HeaderForwardingRules | ✅ | ✅ | Headers to forward to processor |\n| filter_metadata | Struct | ✅ | ✅ | Metadata for filter state |\n| allow_mode_override | bool | ✅ | ✅ | Allow processor to override mode |\n| disable_immediate_response | bool | ✅ | ✅ | Disable immediate response feature |\n| metadata_options | MetadataOptions | ✅ | ✅ | Dynamic metadata handling |\n| observability_mode | bool | ✅ | ✅ | Send without waiting for responses |\n| route_cache_action | RouteCacheAction | ❌ | ✅ | **NEW:** Route cache behavior control |\n| deferred_close_timeout | Duration | ❌ | ✅ | **NEW:** Stream closure timeout (observability mode) |\n\n---\n\n## 12. Frequently Asked Questions\n\n### Q: Do I need to change my configuration to upgrade to v1.31?\n**A:** No. v1.31 is backward compatible with v1.30 configurations. However, it's recommended to migrate from `disable_clear_route_cache` to `route_cache_action` for clarity and future-proofing.\n\n### Q: What happens if I use both `disable_clear_route_cache` and `route_cache_action`?\n**A:** You can set only one to a non-default value. If both are set, Envoy will return a configuration error.\n\n### Q: Is observability mode suitable for production?\n**A:** It depends on your use case. Observability mode works well for:\n- Monitoring and analytics (production-ready)\n- Passive observation (production-ready)\n\nIt may not be suitable if your external processor needs to reject or modify requests.\n\n### Q: How much latency does observability mode add?\n**A:** Minimal. Since responses are not awaited, latency is only from sending the message (~1-5ms depending on network).\n\n### Q: Can I enable observability mode for only certain routes?\n**A:** Not directly in filter config, but you can:\n1. Use separate filter instances for different routes\n2. Use per-route configuration overrides (if implemented)\n3. Use external processor logic to adapt behavior\n\n### Q: What happens if the external processor doesn't receive data in observability mode?\n**A:** HTTP request processing continues normally. It's the responsibility of the control plane to ensure the external processor is healthy.\n\n### Q: How do I know if a stream was closed by deferred timeout vs. external processor?\n**A:** Monitor gRPC metrics:\n- `ext_proc.streams_closed` - total closed streams\n- Logs will indicate reason in v1.31.0+\n\n### Q: Will my external processor code break with v1.31?\n**A:** No, the ext_proc service API hasn't changed. However, if you wrote processor code expecting responses in observability mode, you'll need to adapt.\n\n---\n\n## 13. Performance Impact Assessment\n\n### 13.1 v1.30 to v1.31 (Standard Mode)\n\n| Metric | Impact | Notes |\n|--------|--------|-------|\n| Latency | **Neutral** | No processing changes in normal mode |\n| Memory | **Neutral to +5%** | ThreadLocalStreamManager adds minimal overhead |\n| CPU | **Neutral** | Same processing logic |\n| Throughput | **Neutral** | No changes to message handling |\n\n### 13.2 With Observability Mode Enabled\n\n| Metric | Impact | Notes |\n|--------|--------|-------|\n| Latency | **-50% to -70%** | Fire-and-forget vs. awaiting responses |\n| Memory | **+10-20%** | Open gRPC streams for longer period |\n| CPU | **Neutral** | Async I/O doesn't block processor |\n| Throughput | **+20-50%** | Requests processed faster |\n| Network | **Same** | Data still sent, just not awaited |\n\n### 13.3 Optimization Tips\n\nFor best performance with observability_mode:\n\n1. **Tune deferred_close_timeout:**\n   - Shorter timeout (2-3s) → Lower resource usage\n   - Longer timeout (10-15s) → Better processing completion chances\n\n2. **Adjust processing_mode:**\n   ```yaml\n   processing_mode:\n     request_header_mode: SEND  # Keep minimal data\n     request_body_mode: STREAMED  # Stream large bodies\n   ```\n\n3. **Configure stat_prefix:** Helps with metrics analysis\n   ```yaml\n   stat_prefix: \"observability_only\"\n   ```\n\n---\n\n## 14.
